GT Equivalence Verification (PO35)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v) - omega0**c0*(gamma*Abs(v)**c1 + c2)*x
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed function):
\[
-3.4278620084\,x\,(0.034997753689396\,|v|^{1/3}+1)\;+\;0.100299255716928\sin t\;-\;0.888494670723871\sin v.
\]
So GT has exactly these structural pieces:

1) a pure \(\sin(t)\) term (no \(x\) factor),  
2) a pure \(\sin(v)\) term (no \(x\) factor),  
3) an \(x\) term multiplied by \((1 + k|v|^{1/3})\), i.e.
\[
(-3.4278620084)x \;+\;(-3.4278620084\cdot 0.034997753689396)\,x|v|^{1/3}.
\]
No other dependence (no \(v\), \(v^3\), \(v|v|\), logs, exponentials, etc.).

Also note: \(\cos(t+\phi)\) can match \(\sin(t)\) by phase shift, but **none** of the candidates contain \(\sin(v)\); they contain polynomial/power terms in \(v\), \(v|v|\), etc. A polynomial/power expression cannot equal \(\sin(v)\) for all real \(v\) unless the sine coefficient is 0, but in GT it is fixed nonzero \(-0.88849...\).

Now check candidates.

---

### Candidates 1–8
All have a \(\cos(c+t)\) term, which could be tuned to match \(0.100299\sin t\) (set amplitude and phase).  
But none have any \(\sin(v)\) term. They only have \(v\), \(v^3\), \(v^{c}\), \(v|v|\), \(v\exp(\cdot)\), etc. These cannot reproduce \(-0.88849\sin v\) for all real \(v\). Setting those coefficients to 0 would remove all \(v\)-dependence, but GT still has \(\sin(v)\).  
**So 1–8 cannot match.**

Additionally, their \(x\)-dependent \(v\) coupling is via \(x\log(1+c|v|)\) or \(x v^{c}\), not \(x|v|^{1/3}\) in a linear sum with \(x\). Even if \(\sin(v)\) were present (it isn’t), logs cannot equal a fractional power globally.

---

### Candidates 9–19
These are of the form: linear/polynomial in \(v\), plus \(x|v|\), plus \(v^c x\), plus \(\cos(t+\phi)\), etc. Again:
- No \(\sin(v)\) term at all ⇒ cannot match GT’s \(-0.88849\sin v\).
- Their \(x\)-dependence uses \(x|v|\) or \(x v^c\), not \(x|v|^{1/3}\) plus a separate \(x\) term in the exact GT combination (though you could create an \(x\) term via \(c5 x\), you still can’t create \(x|v|^{1/3}\) unless a \(v^c x\) term uses \(|v|\) specifically; it doesn’t—most are \(v^{c}x\) without Abs, which is not globally equal to \(|v|^{1/3}\) on negative \(v\)).
So **9–19 cannot match.**

---

### Candidate 20
Has \(\cos(t+\phi)\) (OK for \(\sin t\) via phase), has \(x\log(1+c|v|)\) (not \(|v|^{1/3}\)), has \(v|v|\), \(v^3\), and no \(\sin(v)\).  
**Cannot match.**

---

### Candidates 21–23
Same issue: \(\cos(t+\phi)\) can match \(\sin t\), but no \(\sin(v)\). Also \(x\log(1+c|v|)\) cannot equal \(x|v|^{1/3}\) globally.  
**Cannot match.**

---

### Candidates 24–26
Contain \(\cos(t+\phi)\) and \(v^{c}x\) terms (without Abs), plus \(v|v|\). No \(\sin(v)\). Also \(v^{1/3}\) is not real for negative \(v\) unless interpreted specially; GT uses \(|v|^{1/3}\) explicitly, so you’d need Abs. These candidates don’t provide \(x|v|^{1/3}\).  
**Cannot match.**

---

### Candidate 27
Has an extra \(\log(c v+1)\) (not even Abs), plus \(x\log(1+c|v|)\), plus \(v x^2\). No \(\sin(v)\).  
**Cannot match.**

---

### Candidate 28
Has \(x\log(1+c|v|)\) and \(v(c+x)^{p}\). No \(\sin(v)\).  
**Cannot match.**

---

### Candidate 29
Has \(\cos(t+\phi)\), \(x\log(1+c|v|)\), \(v x^2\), and also \(v\cos(c t)\) (time-modulated \(v\) term). Still no \(\sin(v)\).  
**Cannot match.**

---

### Candidate 30–31
Have \(\cos(t+\phi)\), \(x\log(1+c|v|)\), and various \(v^c x\) or \(v/(t+c)^3\). No \(\sin(v)\).  
**Cannot match.**

---

### Candidates 32–39
Include \(\cos(t+\phi)\), \(x|v|\), \(v^3\), \(v^c x\), etc., sometimes extra \(Abs(v)\) alone or \(v\) terms. Still no \(\sin(v)\).  
**Cannot match.**

---

### Candidate 40
Adds \(t(c+v)^5\). No \(\sin(v)\).  
**Cannot match.**

---

### Candidates 41–42
Have \(\cos(t+\phi)\) plus an extra \(x\sin(c t+\phi)\) or \(x\cos(c t+\phi)\). GT has only a *pure* \(\sin t\) term, not multiplied by \(x\), so these extra time-dependent \(x\)-terms must be zeroed (set coefficient 0). Even then, still no \(\sin(v)\).  
**Cannot match.**

---

### Candidate 43
Has \(x\log(1+c|v|)\), \(v x^2\), and \(Max(0,x)^p\). No \(\sin(v)\). Also introduces non-smooth piecewise behavior absent in GT.  
**Cannot match.**

### Candidate 44
Has \(x^{c}\) term and \(v x^2\), plus \(x\log(1+c|v|)\). No \(\sin(v)\).  
**Cannot match.**

---

### Candidates 45–47
Have \(\cos(t+\phi)\), \(x\log(1+c|v|)\), and \(v^c x\) etc. No \(\sin(v)\).  
**Cannot match.**

---

### Candidates 48–49
Contain \(x^3\) or \(x(c+v)^2\) and \(v x^2\). No \(\sin(v)\).  
**Cannot match.**

---

### Candidate 50
Has \(\cos(t+\phi)\), \(x|v|\), \(v^3\), \(v^c x\). No \(\sin(v)\).  
**Cannot match.**

GT contains the nonzero term \(-0.8884946707\sin(v)\). None of the candidates include any \(\sin(v)\) or \(\cos(v)\) term that could be phase-shifted into \(\sin(v)\). No choice of constants can make a combination of algebraic/log/exp terms equal \(\sin(v)\) for all real \(v\). Therefore no candidate can be globally equivalent to the fixed GT.

The `sin(v)` term can be Taylor expanded as `v - v³/6 + v⁵/120 - ...`, but we need EXACT equivalence, not approximations.

**Key observation:** The GT contains `sin(v)`, which is a transcendental function of `v`. Most candidates use polynomial terms in `v` (like `v`, `v³`, `v*|v|`) and/or `log(|v|+1)` terms, but NOT `sin(v)`. 

For exact equivalence, candidates must either:
- Contain `sin(v)` explicitly, OR
- Have some combination that exactly equals `sin(v)` (impossible with polynomials, logs, powers, etc.)

Let me check each candidate for the presence of `sin(v)`:

**None of the candidates contain `sin(v)`.** They all use combinations of:
- `v`, `v³`, `v⁵`, `v*|v|`, `|v|`, `v^c` (power terms in v)

- `x*|v|`, `x*log(|v|+1)`, `v^c * x` terms
- `cos(t+c)` or `sin(t+c)` terms (in t, not v)

Since `sin(v)` cannot be exactly represented by any finite combination of polynomials, absolute values, logarithms, or power functions of `v`, **none of these candidates can match the GT**.

A polynomial like `c1*v + c2*v³ + ...` is only an approximation to `sin(v)`, not an exact equivalence. By Rule 2, asymptotic/Taylor approximations are forbidden.
